<Construct>Simplify the algebraic fraction: \(\frac{6x^2 + 9x}{3x}\)</Construct>
<Question>What is the simplified form of the algebraic fraction?</Question>
<Correct Answer>\(2x + 3\)</Correct Answer>
<Incorrect Answer>\(\frac{6x^2 + 9x}{3}\)</Incorrect Answer>
<Misconception>Cannot identify a common factor when simplifying algebraic fractions</Misconception> 



<Construct>Sketch a line graph representing the journey of a cyclist who accelerates from rest, then travels at a constant speed, before decelerating to a stop.</Construct>
<Question>At what point on the graph is the cyclist travelling at their fastest speed?</Question>
<Correct Answer>The point where the line is horizontal.</Correct Answer>
<Incorrect Answer>The point where the line is steepest.</Incorrect Answer>
<Misconception>Does not realise that a curved line represents a changing gradient</Misconception> 



<Construct>Given the data for the number of hours a group of students spent studying for an exam, calculate the mean and standard deviation</Construct>
<Question>A researcher wants to study the effect of study time on exam performance. They collected data from a sample of 50 students, recording the number of hours each student spent studying. The mean study time was 6.5 hours, and the standard deviation was 1.2 hours. What is the mean study time for all students in the population?</Question>
<Correct Answer>6.5 hours</Correct Answer>
<Incorrect Answer>Cannot be determined from the given information</Incorrect Answer>
<Misconception>Believes 'data' and 'sample' are interchangeable</Misconception>

<Incorrect Answer>\( \sqrt{24} \)</Incorrect Answer>
<Misconception>When comparing non like surds, does not square the surds</Misconception>

<Correct Answer>\(x = 3\)</Correct Answer>
<Incorrect Answer>\(x = 14/5\)</Incorrect Answer>
<Misconception>When substituting into an algebraic term, believes they can disregard the coefficient</Misconception> 



<Construct>A bag contains 5 red marbles, 3 blue marbles, and 2 green marbles.</Construct>

<Correct Answer>1/8</Correct Answer>
<Incorrect Answer>3/10</Incorrect Answer>
<Misconception>Thinks the order of events does not matter in a question about combined probability with no replacement</Misconception>

<Incorrect Answer> \(y = 2x + 4\)</Incorrect Answer>
<Misconception>Believes the y-intercept of a line is the solution to its equation</Misconception> 



<Construct>A pie chart showing the proportion of different coloured cars in a car park.</Construct>
<Question>What is the proportion of red cars in the car park, if the sector representing red cars is 72 degrees?</Question>
<Correct Answer>0.2</Correct Answer>
<Incorrect Answer>1/72</Incorrect Answer>
<Misconception>Believes the proportion for a pie chart sector is 1 divided by the number of degrees</Misconception> 



<Construct>Graph the reciprocal of the function \(y = x^3 + 1\)</Construct>
<Question>What is the equation of the asymptote for the reciprocal function?</Question>
<Correct Answer>\(y = 0\)</Correct Answer>
<Incorrect Answer>\(y = 1\)</Incorrect Answer>
<Misconception>Believes a reciprocal graph comes from a cubic equation</Misconception> 



<Construct>Simplify expressions involving surds</Construct>
<Question>Simplify the expression:  \(3\sqrt{5} \times 2\)</Question>
<Correct Answer>\(6\sqrt{5}\)</Correct Answer>
<Incorrect Answer>\(\sqrt{60}\)</Incorrect Answer>
<Misconception>When multiplying a surd by an integer to write as one surd, squares the number under the surd rather than the number in front</Misconception> 



<Construct>Graph \( y = \frac{1}{x} \) and \( y = \frac{1}{x^2} \) on the same axes.</Construct>
<Question>Which graph represents \( y = \frac{1}{x^2} \)?</Question>
<Correct Answer>The graph that is closer to the x-axis and has a steeper descent towards the origin.</Correct Answer>
<Incorrect Answer>The graph that is further from the x-axis and has a gentler descent towards the origin.</Incorrect Answer>
<Misconception>Confuses the graph of 1/x with 1/x² when both are shown</Misconception> 



<Construct>Calculate population size using the capture-recapture method.</Construct>
<Question>A scientist captures 100 fish from a lake and tags them. They release the fish back into the lake. A week later, they capture 50 fish and find that 10 of them are tagged. Using the capture-recapture method, estimate the size of the fish population in the lake.</Question>
<Correct Answer>500</Correct Answer>
<Incorrect Answer>490</Incorrect Answer>
<Misconception>Believes you subtract the number marked second from the estimated population to find the number marked first when using the capture-recapture method</Misconception>

<Incorrect Answer>40cm²</Incorrect Answer>
<Misconception>Thinks all dimensions given must be used when calculating the area</Misconception>

<Construct>A bag contains 3 red marbles, 2 blue marbles, and 5 green marbles. A marble is drawn at random from the bag and not replaced. A second marble is then drawn at random. </Construct>

<Correct Answer>3/10 * 5/9 = 1/6</Correct Answer>
<Incorrect Answer>3/10 * 5/10 = 3/20</Incorrect Answer>
<Misconception>Believes the probability on all branches travelling in the same direction on a tree diagram are the same, despite changing events</Misconception>
